            <meta property="og:title" content="Fully assembled 3D printable wrench by barspin" />
    <meta property="og:url" content="https://www.thingiverse.com/thing:139268" />
    <meta property="og:type" content="website" />
    <meta property="og:description" content="Please consider supporting me on Patreon: https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree
After watching the infamous video from a few years back where Z-Corp prints a fully working wrench i decided i wanted to do the same thing on my own printer.  
Now, i am not talking about a &quot;print-several-pieces-and-then-assemble&quot; version which there are already a ton of on the internet.
What i wanted to do was something i could print and that would actually be fully working straight out of the printer.
I like to think i came pretty close. All you need to do is to remove the internal support and your done!  
Keep in mind this is a proof of concept, i just wanted to see if i could do it.  
Updated 2013-10-16: Added &quot;Printable Wrench W Longer Screw&quot; which has a longer &quot;screw&quot; (3mm).  
Updated 2013-08-30: I have added two new files. One with a slightly bigger gap between moving parts. This one has 0,55mm gap instead of 0,35mm. Let me know if it works out (in particular with PLA). I have also added a STEP file with no support for anyone who maight want it.  
Here is  a short video: https://youtu.be/Eq_JI3yctJ8  
Experimantal &quot;heavy duty&quot; version: https://www.youmagine.com/designs/printable-wrench-reworked  
Please consider supporting me on Patreon: https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree

By Daniel Nor&eacute;e

<meta name="twitter:title" content="Fully assembled 3D printable wrench by barspin">
<meta name="twitter:description" content="Please consider supporting me on Patreon: https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree
After watching the infamous video from a few years back where Z-Corp prints a fully working wrench i decided i wanted to do the same thing on my own printer.  
Now, i am not talking about a &quot;print-several-pieces-and-then-assemble&quot; version which there are already a ton of on the internet.
What i wanted to do was something i could print and that would actually be fully working straight out of the printer.
I like to think i came pretty close. All you need to do is to remove the internal support and your done!  
Keep in mind this is a proof of concept, i just wanted to see if i could do it.  
Updated 2013-10-16: Added &quot;Printable Wrench W Longer Screw&quot; which has a longer &quot;screw&quot; (3mm).  
Updated 2013-08-30: I have added two new files. One with a slightly bigger gap between moving parts. This one has 0,55mm gap instead of 0,35mm. Let me know if it works out (in particular with PLA). I have also added a STEP file with no support for anyone who maight want it.  
Here is  a short video: https://youtu.be/Eq_JI3yctJ8  
Experimantal &quot;heavy duty&quot; version: https://www.youmagine.com/designs/printable-wrench-reworked  
Please consider supporting me on Patreon: https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree

By Daniel Nor&eacute;e
Home - Things - GooglePlus - Twitter - Facebook - Youtube - Instagram - Vimeo - LinkedIn">

	<script src="/thingiview/js/Thingiview.js?v=2"></script>
	<script src="/thingiview/js/NormalControls.js?v=2"></script>
	<script src="/thingiview/js/Detector.js?v=2"></script>

	<script>
		var target_dom_element = $('.thingiview').get(0);

		// parse opts
		var argv = {};
		var parts = window.location.href.replace(/[?&]+([^=&]+)=([^&]*)/gi, function(m,key,value) {
			argv[key] = value;
		});

		var thingiview = new Thingiview( target_dom_element, 628, 472 );
		if ( parseInt(argv['width']) && parseInt(argv['height']) )
			thingiview.resize( parseInt(argv['width']), parseInt(argv['height']) );

		var animate = function() {
			requestAnimationFrame( animate );
			thingiview.render();
		}
		animate();

		// handle resizes
		window.addEventListener('resize', function() {
			if ( thingiview.fullscreen )
				thingiview.resize(window.innerWidth, 608);
		});

	</script>

                        <div class="thing-page-right">
                            <div class="thing-info">
                                <div id="description" class="thing-info-content">
                                    <h1 class="thing-component-header summary summary">Summary</h1>
<p>Please consider supporting me on Patreon: <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree">https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree</a></p>
<p>After watching the infamous video from a few years back where Z-Corp prints a fully working wrench i decided i wanted to do the same thing on my own printer.  </p>
<p>Now, i am not talking about a &quot;print-several-pieces-and-then-assemble&quot; version which there are already a ton of on the internet.<br>
What i wanted to do was something i could print and that would actually be fully working straight out of the printer.<br>
I like to think i came pretty close. All you need to do is to remove the internal support and your done!  </p>
<p>Keep in mind this is a proof of concept, i just wanted to see if i could do it.  </p>
<p>Updated 2013-10-16: Added &quot;Printable Wrench W Longer Screw&quot; which has a longer &quot;screw&quot; (3mm).  </p>
<p>Updated 2013-08-30: I have added two new files. One with a slightly bigger gap between moving parts. This one has 0,55mm gap instead of 0,35mm. Let me know if it works out (in particular with PLA). I have also added a STEP file with no support for anyone who maight want it.  </p>
<p>Here is  a short video: <a rel="nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/Eq_JI3yctJ8">https://youtu.be/Eq_JI3yctJ8</a>  </p>
<p>Experimantal &quot;heavy duty&quot; version: <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.youmagine.com/designs/printable-wrench-reworked">https://www.youmagine.com/designs/printable-wrench-reworked</a>  </p>
<p>Please consider supporting me on Patreon: <a rel="nofollow" href="https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree">https://www.patreon.com/DanielNoree</a></p>

<h1 class="thing-component-header design how-i-designed-this">How I Designed This</h1>
<p class="detail-video"><iframe src="//www.youtube.com/embed/Eq_JI3yctJ8" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>

                                    
                                    
                                    <h1 class="thing-component-header custom instructions">Instructions</h1>
<ol>
<li>Print  </li>
<li>Remove support using a sharp knife or similar  </li>
<li>Show your friends  =)  </li>
</ol>
<p>Printed on a Replicator at 0,2mm in ABS</p>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I am having a major issue printing this in ABS at 0.2 mm with Simplify3D as my slicer. I cannot seem to get the middle floating portion (the moving jaw part in the slot) to stay in place. I am trying to print this with the regular gap, and even then it seems that the gap is too large (2-3 layers in size at 0.2 mm). I have tried varying bed temp from 105 C to 80 C, and extrusion temp from 235 C to 212C. Also changed extrusion multiplier from 1.00 to 1.10. Nothing seems to do the trick to get that middle printed portion to stay in place. I have failed 7 times now... Not sure what else to do.</p>
<p>Using a well tuned Qidi Tech replicator clone.</p></div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Is the file with the longer screw the design with more clearance added of the one with less?  I want to try with ABS now.  The one I printed with PLA with extra clearance worked ok but it seemed to be too much clearance and it tends to be sloppy and jams up.  I would like less clearance with a longer screw.</p></div>

                <div class="comment-container " id="comment-1140617">

                <div class="comment-body">
    <div class="comment-header">
        <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="/thing:139268#comment-1140617">
                <span title="Jan 15, 2017 10:58 pm">Jan 15, 2017</span>
            </a>

                    </div>
        <a href="/jtinley" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_default_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_default_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/jtinley" class="">jtinley</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Solved! Easy fix for stuck screw! After hours and trying thing on this thread like freezing etc, I finally found a 30 sec trick that worked like a charm.  I used my dremel tool tiniest drill and put a hole through it straight down. then I used that same bit to twist it free and heard it break free. now it turns easily.  I actually used another bit same size diameter just so as not to break the drill bit one.  This is way better solution than mangling the screw with pliers and screwdriver which I also tried. I hope this idea helps someone else having troubles! Thanks for the great design, it's very cool!</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I have just managed to get this to print in PLA I was having problems with the screw not adhering to the bed so had to attach the screw to the body with temporary supports. I found braking the original supports was ok the top one was a but difficult but the body of the wrench was solid, are you using a fan on the print? you definitely need to, it sounds like your bridges are sticking. I'd suggest fan and check your filament diamitor to ensure your layers are bonding properly i did my at 190 C 100% scale my infill was at 80% 0.2 layer height. good luck!</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>So...Just so people know.  All these comment deleted messages are probably because this system is very slow to respond sometimes. Press "save comment" nothing happens for 15-30 seconds.  Press it again.  Nothing. Press it a third time.  Poof!  The comment replicates itself once for each click.  Odd issue but that's why there are "comments deleted" below this one.  </p></div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I'll answer the question first ... no.<br>
I haven't printed so many versions as you but have had similar problems with the three prints I HAVE made in that although I can release the big support structures, I can never get the gear to move at all. Two PLA prints and one ABS and of course I end up throwing them away - big waste of plastic and at the end of the day, money.<br>
I would love this to work ... but I'm afraid that it doesn't on my RepRap machine and it is a machine which only fails with this design. Ho humm!</p></div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>This thing is a pain to keep the screw stuck to the surface. Normally I don't have a problem with small parts but I tried about 5 times before I got it to stick. Both with PLA and ABS on a new Prusa i3 Mk2. Was afraid to get the first layer any closer, may try it once more with the 1st layer squished a little more.</p>
<p>But it's super cool, supports came off just fine and even though the screw wasn't perfect (because the first layer came off after 2 layers) it still worked pretty well. I did scale it up to 105%.</p></div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Thanks for the model!  Printed on PLA and got going the first time (after an hour of prying).</p>
<p>Printrbot simple metal settings:</p>
<p>layer height= .1984<br>
shell thickness = .8<br>
bottom / top thickness = .4<br>
fill density = 15%<br>
speed = 45<br>
temp = 210<br>
platform adhesion = raft</p>
<p>The tabs came out quite easily.  Screw took forever.  Used combination of flat heads and pliers (i think pliers did the trick) and added Vaseline after it got spinning.  </p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">

        <a href="/ejo" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_engineer_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_engineer_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/ejo" class="">ejo</a>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I was able to print this with cheap printer and PLA. Few tips:</p>
<ol><li>There are 3 actually designed parts to remove and you can use force to remove then.</li>
<li>Print as perfect as possible 3DBenchy first, this thing needs good calibration to work.</li>
<li>Once moving, add oil. Even real spanner needs oil and this is much coarser thing if not </li>
<li>Very quick flame treatment with lighter also helps smooth things out.</li>
<li>This desing isn't perfect, so it is hard to make your print perfect either.</li>
</ol></div>
    </span>

                <div class="comment-container " id="comment-565308">
                    <div id="comment-565308-wrapper" class="depth-1">
                <div class="comment-body">
    <div class="comment-header">
        <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="/thing:139268#comment-565308">
                <span title="Feb 14, 2015 6:12 pm">Feb 14, 2015</span>
            </a>

                            <span title="Feb 14, 2015 10:17 pm">- Modified Feb 14, 2015</span>
                    </div>
        <a href="/borgchick" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_engineer_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_engineer_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/borgchick" class="">borgchick</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Printed the "more gap" version using Craftbot, vector slicer, 0.2mm layer height, 25% infill, 90% extruder speed ratio, 50% first layer extruder ratio.  With Craftware's auto supports at 1.5mm @ 65 deg.  Print orientation was flag, as the wrench sits in the photos.</p>
<p>The Craftware added supports broke off easy.  The in-model top and bottom supports took considerably more effort to remove.  This required a lot of tapping with a small flat head screwdriver and hammer.  Actually broke the bottom retainer in trying to free the bottom support.</p>
<p>After the worm gear is still very stuck.  After many hours of tapping with a tiny flat heat screw driver into areas, using an exacto knife, even pouring some acetone onto the gears, I was actually able to turn the worm gear by using a larger flat head screw driver to torque it.  From then on, it was just a lot patience, more cutting around the worm gear, and torqing with various screwdrivers, and finally I am able to turn the worm gear, with EXTREME difficulty.</p>
<p>Sooooo, the moral of the story is, it is not impossible.  But it damn hell is difficult.</p>
<p>And I basically destroyed my thumbs on this.</p>
<p>Oh, ps, the reason the "3D Printed" wording looks like crap is because of a Craftware slicing error, it printed a top cover for those words, so I had to clean that out with the exacto.</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>

    <div class="comment-header">
        <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="/thing:139268#comment-524594">
                <span title="Nov 11, 2014 10:42 am">Nov 11, 2014</span>

                            <span title="Nov 11, 2014 10:51 am">- Modified Nov 11, 2014</span>
                    </div>
        <a href="/L4nce0" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/43/d4/40/6c/a3/2013-04-18_14.14.46_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/43/d4/40/6c/a3/2013-04-18_14.14.46_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/L4nce0" class="">L4nce0</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Heya you asked for PLA feedback.</p>
<p>Well.. Even Cracking the thing in half I literally cannot take out this "support material" it's solid blocks, and would be easier to Drill out. I'm using PLA and I have printed assembled gears before. I did your one with the larger space. The space at the gear is the least of your concerns as it's the most accessible part.</p>
<p>This needs MINOR thin walls, not Blocks for support material. Especially an the bottom. There is no way that would ever come out. PLA is Gooey, you print a solid Block on top, it becomes not 2 parts, but 1. Maybe if I had my fan working, but, with thin walls this would be a no prob print. ABS is better about over the air, shape forming, bridges, than PLA. Honestly with 0 support I probably could have cleaned the few rogue lines up with pliers. Then again, the small part of the wrench is technically fused too. If it was made in a way I could Shim it free (maybe add micro 1 layer tall widely spread out thin walls there too?, but there is a bend in the design, making that strategy impossible. </p>
<p>That's not the biggest thing either. I know it's nice to have it flat, but that's more gravity contact points. Put it on its thin side and only a 2 mm squared section will get fused and need to be shimmed.. Instead of bottom, and top of the larges areas.. </p>
<p>I will note my printer is a high speed mendel max. This was a 30 minute print at about 120 mms. Physical limitations is 150 on this machine, all about calibration to get it to 150. 0.5 mm nozzle, same lh... Meaning I'm running PLA HOT. 200 cel to be exact.<br>
Regards.</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I printed the larger gap model and came out great. It started out like a rusty wrench but after a few minutes of attention it started to glide nice. Very cool design  of custom supports. Thanks.<br>
Printed on replicator2 with PLA<br>
-Supports off  in software</p>
<ul><li>200 micron </li>
</ul></div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>If you have trouble with warping ABS, I have have the perfect solution. Grab some acetone and ABS. Put the ABS in little pieces in an eggcup and fill it with acetone. After 10-20 Minutes the acetone has the same color as the ABS. Grab a Paintbrush and make a thin layer on your !HEATED! build plate. It will smell a bit but it is ok. Then you are Ready for printing.</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I think I know why the author can print one with his Makerbot while Repraps cannot. Correct me if I'm wrong (because I don't have a Reprap), the Makerbot's ReplicatorG software can allow you to do "partial support" while the Reprap's breakaway support material is all or nothing. With "partial support", the Makerbot will make a minimum of supports so that you won't be printing a lot of supports in between the gears. Therefore, you can break free and spin the gears after printing. However, Reprap operators with all or nothing supports will print too much support material so that the gears can't break free. Is this a correct assessment / guess?</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>This thing does not utilise software support. Everything including support structures is done in CAD and is included in the STL file. But there are so many variables that come into play here, type of filament, diameter of filemant, printer/slicer settings, printer, surroundings and so on. As the tolerances might be "on the edge" for some there is not much needed for it to fail.</p></div>

    <div class="comment-header">

            <a href="/thing:139268#comment-428718">

                    </div>
        <a href="/garry_qualls" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_default_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://www.thingiverse.com/img/default/avatar/avatar_default_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/garry_qualls" class="">garry_qualls</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I finally got this printing well in ABS after dealing with a lot of feed problems with the stock mechanism on a Replicator 2X.  I printed the version with the large gaps at the default size and things snapped apart and started working very easily. Very impressive! I am printing with 25% fill and 0.2 mm thickness. I also added some Makerware helper disks under the little pylons that support the break away bits.  Before I did that, they peeled up and broke loose before the fourth layer was complete.  I switched to a different filament (that claimed to be metallic silver but, of course, it's just grey) and noticed that it was significantly harder to remove the plugs and get the screw working. I finally figured out why.  They awesome-wrench-filament was 1.7 mm in diameter and the it's-really-stuck-together wrench was printed with 1.8 mm filament.  It turns out I was supposed to measure the filament thickness and change the filament diameter parameter in the profile!  Who knew?  The feed mechanism/software pushed the same number of centimeters of filament through the nozzle for each print, but the difficult wrench had almost 6% more filament squirted into it - hence the fused gaps. Thanks for the cool part! It's trying to get these cool ones to work that drags everyone through the pain of actually learning how to control these machines properly.</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>As soon as I print one of these, I have a buddy that asks, "Can I have it?".  I've printed five so far.  Although my first one came out perfectly, it may have been beginner's luck.  I've cracked a couple of them while removing the bottom support (the smaller of the two).  And I've noticed in the three that I haven't broken, that the adjustable part of the wrench usually needs a bit of light finger pressure for guidance to keep it from binding up.   There seems to be a bit of slop in it.  Perhaps it's the gaps, but could it also be possible that, if the threaded cylinder that moves up and down within the wrench, were made a little longer, that it would  help to keep the adjustable piece better aligned?  There seems to be a 1/4" of room at the top where it could be lengthened.  This is an awesome design, and if it could be perfected it would be truly amazing.   It is so close now!  I wish that I had the skills to do more than offer suggestions.  Perhaps I will get there someday.</p></div>

It just requires a bit of patience to clean up the raft and supports.    Then I worked the worm gear for a while to get it to operate smoothly.</p></div>

    <div class="comment-header">
        <div class="comment-date">

                    </div>
        <a href="/jmccorm" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/4f/4f/e0/1d/82/joshpic2_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/4f/4f/e0/1d/82/joshpic2_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/jmccorm" class="">jmccorm</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Printed on a Makergear M2 with Simplify3D Creator software on 1.75mm blue ABS from SainSmart. 105C bed, 220C extruder.<br>
No bed tape. Raft was 2 layer, 5mm offset, and 50% infill on the raft to hold the pieces<br>
very steady. Rest of the infill was at 25%. Skirt was 2 layer, 0mm<br>
offset with 2 outlines. Print quality set to High (0.15mm layer height),<br>
top and bottom 3 layers as solid, 2 shells. Bed fan off. No printing issues, but the wrench was locked up tight.</p>
<p>Printed the more gap version, same parameters. I was able to remove the supports. The top clamp was free, but the screw was wedged tight. It just doesn't turn?</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>
    <div class="comment-cards">

    <div class="clear"></div>

    <div id="comment-420051-children" class="comment-children">
                    <div class="comment-container " id="comment-420382">
                    <div id="comment-420382-wrapper" class="depth-2">
                <div class="comment-body">
    <div class="comment-header">
        <div class="comment-date">
            <a href="/thing:139268#comment-420382">
                <span title="Sep 9, 2013 4:01 am">Sep 9, 2013</span>
            </a>

                    </div>
        <a href="/jmccorm" class="avatar-anchor not-for-tiny">
            <img data-cfsrc="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/4f/4f/e0/1d/82/joshpic2_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/4f/4f/e0/1d/82/joshpic2_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>
        <div class="comment-username">
            <a href="/jmccorm" class="">jmccorm</a>
                            - in reply to <a href="/thing:139268#comment-420051" class="comment-parent-author">jmccorm</a>
                    </div>
    </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>I kept working with it. I probably made a good 10 attempts. But this is part of why I went with the Makergear M2. I knew from their high resolution Yoda print that the printer can really shine with a lot of tweaking. Although I think the print itself needs some adjusting on the sides of the screw.</p>
<p>Reduced to a 1 layer outline on the skirt. I adjusted the temperature to 225C for the first layer, then 220C for the rest. I felt that I needed more resolution to get better spacing, so I increased the object size by 50% (making it 9" long) and printed it diagonally on the bed (rotated 290 degrees). I decreased the layer size from .15mm to .12mm. It took some bed tweaking to get a stable print at that size, but arguably, it was worth it. It mostly required adjustment to the bed height (first with the Z access screw, later via the extruder offset in the Simplify3D Creator software) and some fine-tuning on the bed's leveling adjustment screws. The result is that I got that extra resolution, and it made it so where the screw was no longer completely welded to the sides.</p>
<p>Given the amount of effort I've put into this, I might just frame this thing and put it on the well.</p></div>
    </span>
    <div class="comment-cards">
            </div>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>At this point I've given up printing this!</p>
<p>I've printed it two times in blue translucent PLA and once using natural ABS. I have no warp problems, but I have yet had success at breaking off all the supports and getting things moving. I printed the original file and the larger gap file with 3mm PLA @ 0.2mm layer height, 30% infill, 3 perimeters, 205C, heated bed 60C. Both broke when attempting to remove the support. I reprinted in ABS using the larger gap part thinking the greater flexibility of ABS might help: 3mm ABS @ 0.2mm layer height, 30% infill, 3 perimeters, 240C, heated bed 110C.  Broke as soon as I tried freeing the support.</p>
<p>:(</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Hi, just a couple of thoughts, first tho i'd like to comment on the last couple of posts, a fully assembled print with no assembly but some clean up. You could fix your car with it depending on your printer and what its printing with including metal.<br>
OK I actually am here to say about,,parts printed next to each other,,,or a duel color print "and correct me if i'm wrong",,</p>
<p>a .1mm gap is required between a duel color print means the two prints are so close they weld together.<br>
a .2mm gap is a weak weld.<br>
a .3mm gap  is a break away weld.<br>
a .4mm gap is a gap  "this would be my recomended gap between parts so they don't weld together."<br>
a 1mm gap is for sure a gap.</p>
<p>This is based on my Replicator work.<br>
Also unless your printing on a raft,,,sometimes a long abs print curls so i put a birds foot of plastic at the end to help hold it down.<br>
Also i have two raft clamps, they are two strips of metal with bends at each end that grip onto the build plate and hold down the print,,i wait for the raft to print then the first layer of the print to see where it is then put the two clamps on. "my clamps are two peaces of mecano metal strips".</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Let me be clear.  I reduced my Up printer temperature by 25 degrees by NOT USING a 20 buck switch, but soldered inline a 10 ohm resistor and drilled a 3/8 hole on a 45 degree angle in the fan shroud to get a bit of cooling. I figured I didnt want to mess with anything so I made it permanent except for the fact that I soldered a push button across both terminals of the resistor in case I have to check the value.  Its my belief that the measuring component eroded over time, and maybe I would bring that resistance up if it would be required.</p>
<p>Anyway,  everything released just fine.  My only complaint is that the tolerances of the worm assembly are too great.  On the existing model, I would thicken the worm screw's teethus by 5 thousands in every dimension.</p></div>
    </span>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>Hi, Fist off good work, making things that don't require assembly makes sence, i reckon this is the point of machines that are capable of doing it.<br>
I'd like to make a suggestion when making a one print item,,"i know it depends on the printer ,,but,,,,,,link all parts of the first layer with strings,,,so first layer becomes one peace.<br>
Currently there are aprox 8 indervidual parts trying to stick to the build plate, if one breaks off the whole print fails. "i know the strings require cleaning off but for a couple of seconds to pull them off is a small price to pay to improve odds of a successful print."<br>
Thanks tho its a great creation.<br>
Bye for now and be well from Will and Mr Data  :)  :]</p></div>

            <img data-cfsrc="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/fa/ef/82/2f/fb/Perry_the_Platypus_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar" style="display:none;visibility:hidden;"><noscript><img src="https://cdn.thingiverse.com/renders/fa/ef/82/2f/fb/Perry_the_Platypus_thumb_small.jpg" class="comment-avatar"></noscript>        </a>

    <span class="comment-text rendered-markdown">
        <div><p>When slicing this with SF50 I'm getting tons of the following errors:<br>
This should never happen, there is a hole in the triangle mesh, each edge should have two faces.<br>
3999 [2657] [1343, 1345]<br>
Something will still be printed, but there is no guarantee that it will be the correct shape.<br>
Once the gcode is saved, you should check over the layer with a z of:<br>
5.7</p>
<p>I'm going to import it into Netfabb and see if that helps.</p></div>
    </span>
